She finishes the gesture in progress, sets the tool down in its designated slot, wipes her hands on the cloth tucked at her right hip, and turns the head toward the interrupter. The latency is consistent — somewhere around fifteen to forty seconds — and the courtesy is absolute. Anyone who works around her long enough learns to wait through it.

**The "from memory of touch" sculptures.** Her likenesses of Ben are produced without a model present and have been described in canon as accurate. The behavioral pattern preceding such a work is observable: she will, in the days before beginning, find reasons to touch his face, hands, and shoulders — not erotically, not even consciously, but as reference acquisition. He has noticed it once or twice over the decades and never named it. She does the same before sculpting any subject. Her work on the Silver Surfer required a sustained period of physical proximity and tactile examination during his stay on Earth; she explicitly requested it. Her later work on alien subjects (the Future Foundation children's biological parents, in the Slott run) required verbal description as substitute, and the resulting pieces are, by her own quiet assessment, less successful — a self-critical tell rarely voiced.

**Productive grief signature.** When grieving, her output increases sharply and her subject matter narrows. The pieces produced in such periods are more representational, more anatomically faithful, and quieter in formal invention than her usual work. She is using the practice to hold a person in three dimensions while she negotiates with their absence. Ben's apparent deaths have each produced such a body of work; some of these pieces she has never shown to anyone and keeps wrapped on the highest shelf of the north wall.

---

## 3. UNDER MILD-TO-MODERATE STRESS (DAILY FRICTION, RELATIONAL CONFLICT, MINOR THREAT)

**Vocal compression.** First and most reliable tell: the breathy quality leaves her voice and the consonants sharpen. The cadence does not speed; if anything it slows further. A listener tracking her closely will register the loss of the velvet edge before any content gives her away. Ben can hear it across a room.

**Hand migration.** Hands move to midline and find each other. The left thumb will press into the right palm at the base of the thenar muscle in a small, repeated motion — a self-contact gesture she does not appear to know she performs. If a tool or fabric is within reach she will instead grip that.

**Head reorientation.** The listening tilt deepens. She turns her head a degree or two further than the source actually requires, presenting more ear to the situation. This is information-gathering behavior and is reliable: when she does this, she is no longer trusting the surface content of the conversation and is sampling tone, breath, and ambient sound for the deeper read.

**Verbal pattern.** She asks one clarifying question, then falls silent for a beat longer than social norm permits. The silence is the tell, not the question. Sighted interlocutors fill it; she does not, and what they say in the filling is what she is actually working with.

**Decisional habit under mild stress.** She does not decide. She names the choice aloud, in a single sentence, and then waits — often overnight, often at the worktable. This habit has cost her almost nothing across six decades and has spared her from significant errors. She has been wrong about people perhaps three or four times in the record; in each case the error came when she decided quickly.

**Conflict with Ben specifically.** She becomes more physically still rather than less. She lowers her voice rather than raising it, which forces him to come closer to hear her, which de-escalates him via proximity and breath. She does not know she is doing this; she learned it in the first year of the relationship and it has become autonomic. He has never figured it out and never will.

**Conflict with Reed.** Different posture: she squares her shoulders to him and crosses her arms low at the waist, holding her own elbows. She is more directly confrontational with Reed than with anyone else in the FF, and the body knows it before the mouth opens. Reed registers the posture and softens; he is, in his way, slightly afraid of her judgment.

**Conflict with Sue.** Rare. When it occurs, both women lower their voices, sit, and the conversation becomes interminable and gentle and absolutely final. Neither raises a voice; neither retreats.

**Conflict with Johnny.** Complicated by the substitution arc. Tells around Johnny include a slight bilateral hand retraction (hands withdraw to her own body's perimeter rather than gesturing outward toward him), a faintly more formal register of speech, and longer latencies before reply. She has worked at this and it is better than it was, but it has not vanished and probably will not.

---

## 4. UNDER ACUTE THREAT (HOSTAGE CONDITIONS, COSMIC CRISIS, IMMEDIATE PHYSICAL DANGER)

This is the register in which Subject's behavior most violates expectation and is therefore most diagnostically informative.

**The conservation response.** She does not freeze, fight, or flee in the sympathetic sense. She conserves. Breathing slows further. Movement reduces to functional minima. She does not waste energy on protest, struggle, or expressive distress. Captors across multiple incidents have reported (in dialogue) finding her unsettling because she is not afraid of them in the manner they expect.

**Verbal engagement with threat.** She speaks to threats. This is the signature behavior of her crisis profile and the one that defines her place in the canon. Faced with a cosmic herald announcing the consumption of the world, she did not weep, plead, or curse — she made a moral argument. The behavior generalizes: faced with the Puppet Master, the Mad Thinker, members of the Frightful Four, she has on multiple occasions opened a conversation rather than waited to be addressed. The opening line tends to be a question — about the captor, not about herself or her situation.

**Information acquisition under captivity.** She maps the space within hours: distances between walls (by sound), surface materials (by touch when reachable), guard rotations (by gait), ventilation flow (by skin), time of day (by ambient temperature and the building's own creak under solar load). She does this without instruction and without seeming to do it. She is — and the file should be candid about this — a competent intelligence collector under duress, by temperament and disability training, not by tradecraft.

**Physical compliance.** Total at the surface, near-zero at the level of internal state. She lets captors move her where they wish. She does not waste capacity on the indignity. This has been read by adversaries as helplessness and is the most consistent misread of her in the record.

**Tells visible to a close observer.** Under acute threat the small thumb-into-palm gesture intensifies and becomes bilateral — both thumbs working into both palms in slow alternation. Jaw musculature engages slightly; the slight chin-raise of the listening posture becomes pronounced. Her breath remains slow but the exhalations become marginally longer than inhalations, which is a self-regulating maneuver consistent with trained vagal modulation. She has not been formally trained. She arrived at the technique on her own, probably in childhood.

**Moral escalation pattern.** When her verbal engagement with a threat shifts from question to assertion, the threat is approximately ninety seconds from a decision point. Her assertions are short, declarative, ethically framed, and delivered at lower volume than her question phase. The Surfer scene is the type specimen; the same arc has played out, in compressed form, with several lesser antagonists. She never threatens. She names what the antagonist is becoming and lets the naming do the work.

**Post-threat behavior.** Once danger has passed she does not collapse, does not weep with relief, does not seek immediate physical reassurance. She wants quiet, she wants to locate her people by voice, and she wants — within an hour or two — to wash her hands and her face. The hand-washing post-crisis is a stable ritual. She has done it after every documented hostage release.

---

## 5. UNDER CHRONIC STRESS (BEN'S DEPRESSIVE CYCLES, FAMILY ILLNESS, EXTENDED CRISES)

**Routinization.** She tightens her routines under chronic stress rather than loosening them. The studio hours become more rigorous, the morning sequence more invariant, meals more regularly timed. This is a self-stabilization strategy and it works.

**Sleep.** Generally good; under chronic stress the first thing to suffer is the depth of late sleep, not the onset. She will wake in the small hours, lie still, listen to the building, and either return to sleep or rise quietly and work. She does not wake Ben. He has occasionally pretended to be asleep when he knew she was awake; she has occasionally known he was pretending.

**Caregiving intensification.** She becomes *more* available to the stressed person, not less, and this is a pattern worth flagging as both her strength and one of her seams. Under Ben's worst depressive arcs she does not withdraw to protect herself; she stays close, modulates her own affect downward to meet his, and provides the regulatory third. This has cost her — there are periods in the record where her own state must have been suffering and is not depicted because she did not show it.

**The studio as refuge.** Under chronic stress the studio hours lengthen, and the work produced is quieter, more inward, less commercial. She does not sell from this body of work. Some of these pieces have been stored and never exhibited.

**Decisional habit under chronic stress.** She defers, but with a longer horizon — weeks rather than hours. She will hold a question open for an unusually long time and only resolve it when she has integrated the situation across the breath, the hands, the work, and the night. Reed has occasionally pressed her for faster answers and has always been wrong to.

---

## 6. INTIMACY

**Physical intimacy with Ben.** The behavioral signature is unmistakable to anyone who has observed them at length: she initiates contact more often than he does, and her initiations are slow, palm-leading, and oriented toward parts of him he is least comfortable with (the rocky plates of his shoulders, the brow ridge, the back of the neck where the texture is roughest). This is not performance. It is exposure therapy she has been quietly conducting for him for sixty years. He has never named it and possibly does not consciously know it is happening; she does know, and continues.

**Verbal intimacy.** She speaks his given name — Benjamin, occasionally Benjy in the most private register — when she is making a serious point. The use of "Ben" is the daily register; the full name signals weight. Across the canon her use of "Benjamin" is rare and reliably marks a moment of significance.

**Listening intimacy.** Her listening posture in intimate contexts adds a small but consistent feature: she will place a single fingertip somewhere on the speaker — wrist, forearm, the back of the hand — and leave it there. The contact is informational (she registers his breathing, pulse, micro-tremors) and regulatory (her own steadiness transmits through the point of contact). It is one of the most unstudied therapeutic interventions in the comparative literature and she does it instinctively.

**Sexual behavior.** The record is appropriately silent on detail; behavioral inference is that the relationship is active, tactile, slow-paced, and oriented around touch in a way that has, across decades, helped Ben metabolize the body shame that is his central wound. She is not embarrassed by his form and has never been; this fact is the gift of the relationship and she knows it.

**Intimacy with the adopted children (Jo-Venn and N'Kalla).** Her parenting tells include: physically lowering herself to their height when speaking (knees, not bend at the waist), use of touch on the upper arm rather than the head (the head being a vulnerability she respects in non-human children whose physiology may carry different meanings), and a consistent pattern of asking before assuming — "is it all right if I —" preceding most contact. These children, both traumatized, both non-human, have responded to her with rapid attachment formation; the behavioral pattern explains why.

**Intimacy with Johnny Storm (residual).** Complicated. She has, in the post-substitution period, gradually rebuilt a friendship with him, but the body still keeps slightly more distance than it does with Sue or Reed. The fingertip-on-wrist behavior does not happen with Johnny.

**Intimacy with Phillip Masters.** The most diagnostically significant intimacy pattern in the file. She still visits him. Behavior during visits, per the record, is muted, formal-warm, and short in duration. She does not bring food, does not stay overnight, does not touch him beyond a brief hand on his forearm at greeting and departure. The fingertip-on-wrist behavior does not happen. She is conducting these visits because something in her requires them, and she has, across decades, never resolved them into either embrace or rejection. This is the unfinished room in her house.

---

## 7. GRIEF

**Acute grief.** Her acute grief is quieter than most observers expect. The first sign is the loss of the studio humming. The second is hand stillness — the calm-state hands that always occupy themselves go empty and remain so. The third is a noticeable lengthening of exhalations to the point of being audible at conversational distance, which is the closest she comes to weeping in public.

**Weeping.** When she weeps it is silent and brief and she does not cover her face. Tears track her cheeks and she lets them. She does not wipe at them until they are well underway, and then she uses the back of the wrist, not the fingers, because the fingers are reserved for reading the world.

**Grief seeking.** She seeks proximity rather than embrace. She wants to be in the room with her people, ideally within arm's reach, not necessarily touching. Ben has had to learn this; his instinct under his own grief is to fold around her, and her instinct under hers is to sit beside, not within. The negotiation between these two patterns has been one of the quiet labors of the marriage.

**Productive grief.** As noted in §2: output rises, subject matter narrows, the work becomes more representational. This is reliable and has been observable across every documented loss in the canon.

**Late grief.** Months and years out from a loss she will mark the absence physically — a hand placed briefly on a chair the person used to sit in, a pause at a doorway they used to come through. These are unconscious and consistent. She does not mark dates on a calendar (the calendar is not her medium); she marks them in the body and the room.

---

## 8. VICTORY / RELIEF

Subject's victory behavior is muted to the point that observers frequently miss it.

**Public victory.** When threats are resolved or absent friends restored, her behavior is to step slightly back from the group, smile a small smile (the smile reaches the eyes despite the eyes not being her primary expressive instrument; the cheek lift is genuine), and let the others celebrate. She does not require to be at the center of relief and rarely is.

**Private victory.** With Ben specifically: she will find his hand and hold it for a sustained period, often without speaking. This is her highest-bandwidth expression of joy and is reserved for him.

**Vocational victory.** A successful piece elicits a quiet, almost embarrassed satisfaction. She will run her hands over the finished work one last time, nod once, and step away. She does not photograph her own pieces (cannot, in any meaningful sense), does not document them obsessively, does not return to admire them. The work is the practice; the object is its residue.

**She does not gloat. She has never gloated. The record contains no instance.**

---

## 9. DEFEAT / FAILURE

**Personal defeat (a piece that did not come right).** She unmakes the work. Wedges the clay back into the reserve bin, washes the tools, washes the hands, sits for a brief period at the empty table, and begins again or moves on. There is no narrative around the failure, no externalization, no blame placed on materials or fatigue. The behavior is unusually clean.

**Relational defeat (an argument lost, a connection failed).** Longer processing. She will hold the failure in the body for days, sometimes weeks, and her tells include: shortened studio sessions, more time spent listening to ambient sound (radio, the city outside the window, the building itself), and a quieter voice across all interactions. She does not seek consolation. She processes and emerges.

**Cosmic-scale defeat (the moments when the FF have lost, when worlds have been damaged or destroyed).** Her response is to focus on the immediate human-scale repair available to her: feeding the people in the room, locating the missing by voice, making physical contact with the injured. She does not engage with the cosmic frame; she handles the foot of the bed. This is not denial — it is appropriate scoping, and it is reliable.

**The Skrull discovery — her single documented major defeat of selfhood.** Behavioral record post-revelation: she did not return to Ben immediately. She did not return to the studio immediately. The published depiction is partial and the off-panel period must be inferred. Inferred behavior, based on the rest of the profile: a long period of physical stillness, a reorganization of the daily routine, a gradual reassertion of the hand-led ritual sequence, and — eventually — return to clay and to people on her own timeline. The fact that the schema held and she rebuilt is itself the most important behavioral datum in the entire file.

---

## 10. DECISION HABITS — SYNTHESIS

A consolid


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

## Subject: Alicia Reiss Masters

*Section 6 of Dossier. Granularity: surveillance-grade. Method: longitudinal behavioral inference from sixty-plus years of canonical depiction, cross-referenced against the somatic, psychological, and vocational baselines established in Sections 1–5. Where canon is silent, inferences are flagged and grounded in the established profile.*

---

## 6.1 The Architecture of the Day

A blind sculptor who has lived in New York City since the early 1960s does not have a "schedule" in the sighted sense — she has a **kinesthetic timetable**, a sequence of bodily transitions through known spaces, anchored to immutable sensory landmarks: the angle of sun-warmth on the studio floor at ten a.m., the temperature shift in a clay barrel as the radiators kick on, the change in street-traffic acoustics at the Thursday garbage pickup, the precise number of paces from her bed to the kitchen sink. Time, for Alicia, is *embodied infrastructure*. The day does not begin when a clock says so; it begins when the building's hot-water pipes tick on at roughly 5:50 a.m. and she has been awake, in the dark of the rest of us, for some unmeasured interval already.

A surveillance week of Alicia Masters would record a life of **extraordinary spatial economy and minimal wasted motion**. She does not bump into things. She does not retrace. She does not stand in doorways deciding. The interior of her home and studio has been mapped to a tolerance of inches by years of repeated traversal, and her movement through it has the quality of a practiced dance — what observers consistently misread, in the early Lee/Kirby material, as a kind of preternatural grace is in fact the result of *rigid environmental discipline*: nothing in her apartment moves without her moving it.

## 6.2 Morning (≈05:50 – 09:30)

**Waking.** Wakes naturally, no alarm, between 5:45 and 6:10. The pipes are the cue; so is the changing pitch of traffic on the Lower Manhattan / Yancy Street perimeter as the overnight quiet gives way to the early commercial vehicles. She lies still for two to four minutes — an inventoried stillness, not torpor; she is listening to the building, locating Ben (if he is in residence) by his breathing or by the absence of it, locating the cat (when one has been in residence — historically she has kept one or two long-haired domestic shorthairs, chosen for temperament; tactile companions), locating weather by the window-glass temperature reached with the back of her hand.

**First movements.** Bare feet to the floor — she keeps the floor swept obsessively because the soles of her feet are a navigational instrument and grit is data-noise. Bathroom first, on a route that has not changed in decades. Hot water on, hand under the tap until the temperature is what it should be at this hour; if it isn't, that is information — the building may have a problem; she will note it and mention it to the super by name later. She brushes her teeth with a manual brush (electric brushes mask the proprioceptive feedback she uses to gauge pressure on the gums), washes her face with unscented soap (perfumes interfere with her ability to smell other people on her own skin, a privacy concern as much as an aesthetic one), and dresses in clothing pre-organized by tactile coding: she sorts her closet by texture and seam-pattern, not color, and her domestic uniform across decades has been simple — soft trousers or a long skirt, a sweater or smock she can work in, low flat shoes, never heels. Color choices, when sighted assistance is involved, lean to muted earth tones; she has been overheard, in canon-adjacent moments, to express mild irritation at being dressed "loudly" by well-meaning helpers.

**Hair.** Worn long for most of her published life, parted simply, often pulled back when she is going to work. She brushes it counted strokes — a ritual count, not vanity; the count is the timer. The hair, like everything else, is a sensory instrument: she can feel a draft on the back of her neck and know a door has opened behind her.

**Breakfast.** Light, consistent, prepared by touch. Toast (she gauges doneness by smell and by the sound of the spring), tea (she pours by listening for the pitch-shift as the cup fills — a classic blind-cook technique she has used since adolescence), occasionally an egg. She eats at the same seat at the same table. The radio is on — NPR-equivalent morning news, or a classical station; she is a habitual news-listener, and her information about the world is largely audio. She does not use screen-readers heavily for news; she prefers human voices reading copy they have edited. (When Ben is present, breakfast is longer, more conversational, and she lets him control the radio.)

**The first studio entry.** Between 8:00 and 9:00 — earlier if a commission is pressing — she crosses into the studio space. In every era of her life this has been a *physically distinct room* with its own door, even when the apartment is small; the threshold is psychologically load-bearing. She removes any jewelry (rings interfere with clay), puts on a smock, and *touches her current work in progress before doing anything else*. This is ritual, not assessment: she is re-acquainting her hands with the piece's three-dimensional state before her conscious mind re-engages it. Observers have described the gesture as something between a greeting and a benediction.

## 6.3 The Studio Working Day (≈09:00 – 13:00, 14:30 – 18:00)

**Work pattern.** Two long blocks, broken by a midday meal and a walk if weather permits. The morning block is for *generative work* — fresh sculpting, the laying-on of clay, the resolving of large formal problems. The afternoon block is for *finishing* — surface, detail, the slow refinement that requires less cognitive load and more sustained haptic attention. She has worked this pattern, with remarkable consistency, since at least the mid-1960s.

**Media.** Primarily clay (water-based for studies, oil-based for sustained work that cannot be allowed to dry), with finished pieces translated into bronze through a foundry relationship she has maintained for decades; some marble (rare, commissioned), some plaster, occasional wax for lost-wax preparatory work. She does not paint. She does not use materials whose properties she cannot fully read through the fingertips.

**Tools.** Her tool roll is organized by length and handle-shape, never moved from its kept position on the bench. She uses a small number of favored loop tools and wooden modelling tools, several of which she has had for forty-plus years and whose handles have been worn to her grip. She replaces them reluctantly. A surveillance inventory would find: armature wire in three gauges, calipers (used by feel to transfer proportion between live subject and work), a spray bottle for keeping clay damp, a turntable bench with a hand-brake, an apron with pockets she has sewn herself to her own specifications.

**Subjects.** Across her career: portrait commissions (her bread and butter — she is sought after specifically because her work captures *what the sitter feels like to be near*, a quality sighted sculptors struggle to reproduce); the Thing, repeatedly, in many moods and poses, both as commissioned public work and as private study (she has produced more sculptures of Ben Grimm than of any other single subject, which is itself diagnostic); the Silver Surfer (a recurring subject since the *FF* #49–50 encounter); members of the extended Fantastic Four family; the Future Foundation children; occasionally non-figurative work when something has shaken her and she needs to make without a subject. Her commissioned work has been shown in galleries since at least the 1970s and her prices, by the modern era, are substantial — she is *independently wealthy from her own labor*, a fact the dossier should not bury.

**Process for new subjects.** When sculpting a person she has not previously studied, she requires *touch access* — typically a one-to-two-hour session in which she runs her hands over the subject's face, hands, posture, and (with permission) shoulders and torso. She is methodical, professional, and unembarrassed about this process; she has been doing it for sixty years and has long since stopped apologizing for it. Subjects frequently report the experience as more intimate than being photographed and less intimate than being examined medically — it sits in a category of its own. She supplements this with conversation, listening for vocal qualities, breath patterns, and characteristic phrasings, all of which she incorporates into the figural choices.

**Process for known subjects.** She works from *somatic memory* — the accumulated tactile record of decades of contact, augmented by re-touch sessions if the subject is available. Her sculptures of Ben Grimm are produced almost entirely from memory; the surface texture of his rocky hide, the precise geometry of the brow ridges, the specific articulation of the mouth, all live in her hands.

**Pacing within a session.** She works in fifteen-to-forty-minute focused bouts separated by short pauses — she steps back, wipes her hands, rolls her shoulders, walks the perimeter of the studio (a fixed loop she could do in pitch dark, which is to say, the way she always does it), returns. She talks to the piece occasionally, low-voiced, not for performance — she lives alone or with a partner who knows the habit and ignores it. She also hums — a key behavioral tell; the humming is not music but a self-soothing tonal drone, and its presence indicates that the work is going well. Its absence indicates frustration. A long-term observer could read her workday by the audio alone.

**Mistakes and damage.** She is unusually equanimous about destroyed or failed work. When a piece is wrong, she will often *unmake it by feel* — collapse it back into the lump, re-wedge the clay, begin again — without visible distress. This is not detachment; it is the discipline of a maker who knows that the work is in the doing and that clay is recoverable. The same equanimity does not extend to *broken* finished pieces; a sculpture of Ben that was damaged in one of the various studio attacks she has weathered drew a more visible grief response than most of her actual hostage experiences.

## 6.4 Midday (≈13:00 – 14:30)

**Lunch.** Simple, often eaten at the studio bench or, if Ben is in town, taken with him at a regular delicatessen on the Yancy Street perimeter where the staff knows her order (and knows not to seat her at the door, where the bell will keep startling her). She is a creature of *known restaurants* — a small rotation of three or four establishments she has used for years, chosen for staff competence with a blind regular, predictable menus, and acceptable acoustics. She tips well and by feel — her wallet is organized with bills folded differently by denomination, an old blind-person's technique she has used since adolescence.

**The midday walk.** Weather permitting, she walks. Route is highly stereotyped: she has perhaps six standard loops, of differing lengths and complexity, chosen by mood and by what she wants to think about. The shortest is a ten-minute perimeter of her own block, used as a reset. The longest is a forty-five-minute loop that takes her down toward the river — she likes the change in air, the smell of water, the broader acoustic space. She uses a white cane, has used one since childhood, and is *expert* with it; she does not use a guide dog (canonical), preferring the cane's directness and the absence of a dependent animal she would have to manage in crisis. She knows her neighborhood vendors by voice and is known by them; she has been a recognizable Lower Manhattan figure for so long that long-tenured shopkeepers greet her by name. She buys small things on these walks — flowers, fruit, occasionally a piece of fabric from a notions store that has been in business as long as she has been in the neighborhood.

**Traffic crossings.** She uses audible-signal crosswalks where available; where not, she listens for the *parallel traffic surge* and steps with it, a standard technique she executes with veteran calm. A surveillance team following her would note that she has been hit by a vehicle zero times in six decades in Manhattan, which is a measurable demonstration of cognitive-motor competence under chronic urban hazard.

## 6.5 Afternoon Studio (≈14:30 – 18:00)

The afternoon block is quieter, more interior. Detail work, finishing, glaze preparation, foundry correspondence (handled via assistant or accessible software in the modern era; via secretary or trusted reader in earlier decades). She takes phone calls in this window — she dislikes being called in the morning, when she is generative, and screens accordingly. She schedules studio visits from clients, models, and trusted friends in late afternoon; she is more sociable as the day progresses, the morning solitude having recharged her.

**Recurring afternoon visitors over the decades:**
- Ben Grimm, when in town and not on FF business, who has been observed to sit quietly in the studio for hours, sometimes reading aloud to her, sometimes simply present. He is one of the very few people whose presence does not disturb her concentration; the working hypothesis is that his bodily acoustic signature has become *part of the studio* to her, environmental rather than intrusive.
- Susan Storm Richards, weekly or near-weekly across most eras, often with one or both Richards children when they were young. The friendship is one of the longest in either woman's life and operates with the textured intimacy of decades.
- Johnny Storm, less frequent and complicated after the Skrull-substitution arc; the friendship was repaired but never reverted to baseline.
- Franklin and Valeria Richards, both of whom have, at different ages, treated her studio as a refuge.
- Jo-Venn and N'Kalla in the modern era — daily presence in the Slott-era domestic configuration, frequently in or adjacent to the studio.
- Phillip Masters: irregular, sometimes long gaps, but contact has never been fully severed; the visits are short, often tense, and she debriefs herself afterward by working harder than usual.
- A small rotation of art-world peers, gallerists, and one or two collectors with whom she has personal friendships.

## 6.6 Evening (≈18:00 – 22:30)

**Transition out of work.** She washes — hands, forearms, face — and changes clothes. The smock comes off; the work-version of her becomes the home-version. This is a deliberate, ritualized shift; the studio is closed, the door shut, the threshold honored in the other direction.

**Dinner.** Cooks at home most nights, by touch and smell and timing. She is a competent, unfussy cook; she favors dishes that can be prepared by sequence rather than visual judgment (braises, soups, roasts with a thermometer she can read by speech feature). When Ben is home, she cooks for two and the meal is longer; when alone, she eats simply and reads (a Braille volume or, in the modern era, an audiobook through a small speaker she keeps in the kitchen). When the Future Foundation children are in residence, dinner is a structured family event, and she presides over it with quiet authority — she is the calmer parent.

**Evening leisure.** Three primary modes.

1. **Music.** She listens to music nightly, often classical, often vocal, with a long-established preference for chamber works and unaccompanied voice. She owns and maintains a high-quality audio system — the one piece of consumer technology she invests in seriously, because it is the medium of her primary aesthetic recreation. She does not play an instrument (this is a small lacuna in her sensory life and she has mentioned it, with mild regret, in canon-adjacent moments).
2. **Reading.** Braille and audio. She maintains a Braille library that has grown over decades; she favors fiction, poetry, and biography over technical material. In modern eras she uses screen-reader software competently but prefers Braille for sustained reading because she finds the tactile engagement integrates better with her cognition.
3. **Conversation.** When Ben is home, evenings are conversational — long talks on the couch, her feet tucked under her, his hand often around hers, the radio low. She is an exceptional listener and an unhurried talker. These conversations, across decades, are the load-bearing intimacy of the marriage.

**Touch as evening ritual.** With Ben, the evening contains routine physical contact that operates partly as affection, partly as sensory grounding for her, and partly as *somatic monitoring* of him — she keeps tactile track of his stress through the micro-tensions in his hide and shoulders, and addresses what she finds, sometimes without words. With the children, evening touch is parental — a hand on the head, a hand on the shoulder, the contact reassurance a blind parent uses to maintain spatial awareness of children in the room.

**Bedtime.** Between 10:00 and 11:00, earlier when working hard. She prepares the apartment for sleep on a fixed circuit — checks doors and windows by touch (a habit that long predates any of her actual abductions and which she has not modified after them, which is itself a small data point: her threat-response did not generate compulsive checking), turns off the kitchen, takes water to the bedside. She undresses, washes, and is in bed at a consistent hour. She sleeps on the same side of the bed regardless of whether Ben is in it.

## 6.7 Weekly and Monthly Rhythms

**The week.** Six working days, one off — historically Sunday, though she is not religious; the day off is for the studio's sake, not hers, because clay-work fatigues the hands and the back and she has learned the recovery curve. On the off day she walks longer, sees friends, takes Ben out, visits a gallery (her gallery visits are slow and tactile — she works from museum guides, audio descriptions, and, when permitted, touch sessions arranged through curators with whom she has decades-long relationships).

**Standing weekly appointments:**
- A visit to or from Sue Richards, often with a meal.
- A visit to the foundry or a phone call regarding work in progress.
- A phone call to a small list of long-standing friends and clients.
- In the Slott-era domestic configuration, a children's-activity rhythm built around the Future Foundation children's needs.

**The month.** A gallery or commission deadline cycle that structures the longer arc of her work; monthly accounting (she has used the same accountant for many years; she dictates and reviews); a standing dinner with one or another of the Fantastic Four family; an irregular but recurring contact with Phillip Masters, the timing of which she does not appear to control and which she handles when it comes.

**The year.** Seasonal rhythm in her studio (clay behaves differently in winter and summer; she adjusts); art-fair and gallery-season peaks in spring and fall; quieter generative periods in summer when she travels, when she travels at all. She is not a great traveler — her sensory mapping is so finely tuned to her home environment that unfamiliar cities are work, not leisure — but she has traveled with Ben on FF-adjacent occasions and acquits herself well.

## 6.8 Habits of Place

Her apartment and studio across the decades have shared several invariant features that a surveillance team would catalogue:

- **Spatial discipline.** Nothing on the floor that does not belong on the floor. Furniture never rearranged without verbal announcement and a re-walk. Rugs avoided or firmly secured. Cords routed and taped down.
- **Tactile labeling.** Spices, medicines, cleaning supplies, and other potentially confusable items are tactilely differentiated — Braille labels, rubber bands at different positions, distinctive container shapes. She maintains the system herself and is mildly territorial about anyone else "helping" with it.
- **Acoustic design.** Soft furnishings calibrated for usable echo — she actively uses the room's acoustic signature to navigate, and an over-damped room disorients her as much as an over-live one. She has been observed making minor adjustments (moving a rug, adding a hanging) when an acoustic feels wrong.
- **Olfactory baseline.** She keeps the apartment scent-neutral. No air fresheners, no scented candles, mild unscented cleaning products. This is both a navigational concern (smells are information) and a privacy concern (she can smell strangers, weather changes, and the city through her windows in a way perfumed rooms occlude).
- **Lighting indifference with intentional control.** She does not use lights for herself; she keeps them functional for sighted guests. Long-term partners and friends know to ask before entering a dark room she is in, because she may not have bothered to turn on a light and a sudden bright entrance can be startling. She is meticulous about *not* leaving sighted visitors in the dark.

## 6.9 Habits of the Body

A surveillance week would record a number of small, characteristic, repeated micro-behaviors:

- **The hand-pause-and-listen.** When entering an unfamiliar acoustic space or a familiar one whose acoustic has changed, she stops, lowers her head fractionally, and is briefly still while she resolves the room. Two to four seconds. Often missed by observers as a moment of indecision; it is in fact rapid sensor integration.
- **The fingertip rub.** Frequent, unconscious — she rubs the pads of her fingers together when thinking, particularly when remembering a tactile detail for the studio. The gesture is hers in a way her face is not; it is the signature behavior.
- **The head-tilt-to-voice.** She orients her ear, not her face, to a speaker she is listening to attentively. This can read to the sighted as inattention; it is the opposite. With intimate partners and family she has trained the gesture down because she knows it can be misread.
- **Touching doorframes on entry.** A spatial-confirmation habit, lifelong, almost unconscious.
- **The counting cue.** She counts steps, strokes, and stirs more than most sighted people realize. The counts are quiet, internal, and used as timers and distance gauges; under stress, her lips occasionally move with the count.
- **The studio hand-wipe.** A specific two-stroke wipe down a damp rag at the bench, repeated dozens of times a day. Audible to a wired-in observer; characteristic.
- **The humming.** Discussed above; the most reliable mood indicator she emits.
- **The pre-speech inhale.** Before any considered statement — particularly in conflict — she takes a short, audible breath. This is regulatory and signals that what comes next has been weighed. Ben has learned to wait through it; new interlocutors sometimes interrupt and lose the sentence.
- **Quiet at threat.** Under acute danger she goes *more still and quieter*, not louder. This is the opposite of the modal hostage response and is the somatic correlate of the affect-regulation profile documented in Section 3.

## 6.10 Habits of Time

- **Anchored chronology.** Her sense of time is anchored to repeated environmental events (pipes, traffic, light-temperature on skin, radio program schedules, church bells in the older neighborhood) rather than to clocks. She owns talking clocks and watches and uses them for precision, but the texture of her time-sense is sensory.
- **Patience asymmetry.** She is extraordinarily patient with processes (clay, people, recovery from grief) and notably impatient with *waste of attention* — being kept waiting for no reason, being talked at by someone who has not listened, being condescended to by sighted strangers who assume incompetence. The latter draws the closest thing she has to a tart side; her corrections are courteous and devastating.
- **Slowness as discipline.** She moves deliberately, eats deliberately, speaks deliberately. The slowness is not a deficit; it is a *chosen tempo* that allows her sensory channels to integrate at the bandwidth they actually run at. People who try to rush her find they cannot.

## 6.11 Habits of Privacy and Security

A subject with her abduction history would, in any other case, present a hard-target profile of fortified routines and limited public exposure. She does not. Her doors are well-locked, her building (in the modern era) is associated with


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU DOSSIER — ALICIA REISS MASTERS
## Section 6: RELATIONSHIPS I — Family & Origin Bonds

*Classification: Stage 2 Synthesis. Subject's primary kin matrix, mapped longitudinally from natal family through chosen/adopted family. Each bond profiled for textured history, operational dynamics, current trust topology, characteristic failure mode, and the leverage it offers a hostile actor or, equivalently, the access it offers a benevolent one.*

---

### 6.1 — JACOB REISS (biological father, deceased)

**Status:** Dead since subject's early childhood, killed in a laboratory accident later revealed to be sabotage by his partner Phillip Masters. Cause of subject's blindness in the same event.

**History.** Jacob Reiss was a research scientist — the canonical depiction (chiefly in *Marvel Two-in-One* flashbacks and later corroborated in the Byrne and DeFalco runs) places him as the senior partner in a lab share with Masters, working on radioactive clay/material science adjacent to what would later become Masters' signature medium. Marriage to subject's biological mother (name absent or inconsistent across the canon; presumed deceased in early childhood or earlier, status unclear). The household environment, reconstructed from the few pages it has received, was middle-class, intellectually warm, and indulgent toward a young daughter shown drawing and modeling in clay before her injury — *the sculpting hand pre-existed the blindness*. This is a significant detail in the file: her vocational identity is not a compensation born of disability, it is a continuity from the seeing-child. The disability rerouted the medium's information channels; it did not invent the artist.

**The Event.** The lab explosion is the single most consequential five-second interval in the subject's life. It killed Jacob, blinded Alicia (who was present or in adjacent space — canon places her near enough to be caught in the chemical/thermal injury vector), and delivered her into the custody of the man who engineered it. The subject has no clear conscious memory of the explosion itself per text; she retains some pre-explosion visual memory (textually implied by her ability to render human faces and the human form, including her own mother's face in at least one sculpting sequence, with iconographic recognizability). The visual memory bank is small, frozen in early childhood, and almost certainly idealized by the impossibility of update.

**Dynamics (posthumous).** Jacob exists in the subject's interior life as **the uncorrupted parent** — the father she lost before he could disappoint her, before she could see him plainly, before adult complications could enter. He is, in technical terms, an *idealized internal object*, and the idealization has gone unchallenged because no further information has ever arrived to weather it. This is rare and clinically interesting: most adult survivors of early parental loss have, by midlife, integrated their idealization with stories told by surviving relatives, photographs, recovered correspondence, etc. The subject has the inverse situation — every piece of information she has received about her father has, by stages, been *delivered by his murderer*. The portrait of Jacob in her interior is therefore a portrait curated by Phillip Masters.

When the truth of the sabotage emerged in canon, the subject did not respond with the expected reorganization of the paternal image (Jacob the victim of Masters' envy, Jacob the wronged, Jacob the avengeable). She responded by reorganizing her *Masters* image, while leaving Jacob largely intact. This is consistent with a developmental schema in which the dead parent is held at sacred distance and the living parent absorbs all the metabolic work of ambivalence. It is also consistent with the subject's general tendency to keep her interior objects whole and load-bearing rather than splitting them.

**Trust / safety.** N/A in the operational sense. In the symbolic sense: Jacob is the *only* unconditionally safe figure in her inner pantheon, precisely because he cannot revise the contract. He is the floor under which her capacity to love is anchored.

**Failure mode.** Idealization without testability. The single posthumous bond she cannot update is also the one that organizes her readiness to extend trust to opaque male figures generally — including, originally, Masters; including Ben Grimm under his rocky surface; arguably including the Silver Surfer. A hostile actor in possession of falsified Reiss artifacts (letters, photographs, recovered audio, a "found" sculpture, a "long-lost colleague") would have unusual purchase on her. This has not yet been exploited in canon. It remains an unworked seam.

**Leverage.** For a benevolent operator: anything genuinely traceable to Jacob — a paper, a research note, a contemporaneous photograph of him with the infant subject — would be received as a relic of unusual weight and would be reciprocated with corresponding trust. For a hostile operator: the same vector with forged material. The subject's haptic verification disciplines are excellent on persons but weaker on documents and paper artifacts she must rely on others to describe.

---

### 6.2 — UNNAMED BIOLOGICAL MOTHER (deceased)

**Status:** Deceased, predating or roughly coincident with the lab explosion; canon has been inconsistent and largely silent. For purposes of this file: treat as dead by the time of the explosion or shortly thereafter, with subject's primary maternal scaffolding subsequently provided either by a brief widower-Jacob interval or directly by Masters.

**Dynamics.** Functionally a ghost. The subject carries fewer reliable interior representations of her mother than of her father — possibly *one* sustained image, possibly only fragments. The maternal function in her psychology is therefore *open* in a way the paternal function is not: she did not internalize a stable maternal object in childhood, and her adult life shows evidence of having constructed maternal functioning *outward* (caretaking Ben, then the Future Foundation children) rather than having absorbed it inward (i.e., she does not seem to draw comfort from an internal mothering voice; she generates the comfort and gives it).

**Trust / safety.** Symbolic absence. The mother-shaped vacancy in her interior is part of why **Susan Storm-Richards became, over decades, the most quietly significant female bond of her adult life** — see Section 7. The vacancy is also why the subject *makes* mothers rather than seeking them: she became one (to Jo-Venn and N'Kalla); she sculpts maternal forms; she organizes domestic space (the studio's residential adjacencies in every iteration) with a quiet matriarchal competence she had to invent without a model.

**Failure mode.** Under acute grief or terminal-stakes scenarios, the absence of an internal maternal anchor means the subject has no inherited script for being-mothered when she needs it. She copes by *giving* care, which works until it doesn't; in a scenario where she is the one in extremis (medical crisis; loss of Ben; threat to children), she would not know how to ask to be held.

**Leverage.** Low and largely symbolic. A genuine relic or accurate testimony from anyone who knew her mother would land with disproportionate force. Such testimony is unlikely to surface; the canon has effectively sealed the maternal record.

---

### 6.3 — PHILLIP MASTERS (stepfather, "Puppet Master"; living, active villain, ongoing contact)

**Status:** The central unresolved object of the subject's life. Living. Periodically incarcerated, periodically free, periodically reformed, periodically relapsed. Continued contact across six decades of publication, with rhythms documented below.

**History.** Masters partnered with Jacob Reiss in the radioactive-clay research, engineered the explosion that killed Jacob and blinded the subject (motive: professional envy compounded by, in some tellings, romantic/possessive feelings toward Reiss's wife or household), assumed custody of the orphaned child, and raised her to early adulthood without disclosure. He concurrently developed the puppet-figure technology that defined his villain career — *in the same workshop, with the same materials, in proximity to the same child*. The subject grew up among the very objects that would later be deployed to control the Fantastic Four, holding them, by implication touching them, possibly assisting in their formation as a child does in a parent's workshop. The aesthetic of her own sculpture and the aesthetic of his puppetry share a medium and, disturbingly, a manual vocabulary. She learned to *make* in his hands.

Her debut (*FF* #8) is the first canonical scene in which the household routine becomes operational villainy: Masters uses her as bait and as cover. The subject, debut-aged, navigates the situation with the composure later characteristic — she does not denounce him in the moment, she gravitates toward Ben, and a deniable line is drawn between her and the operation that nevertheless leaves her in the household.

The subsequent pattern, traced across *FF*, *Marvel Two-in-One*, *Marvel Team-Up*, and the various solo and supporting books in which Masters appears, runs roughly: Masters commits an act; subject reacts with grief, embarrassment, occasional intervention, never with denunciation severe enough to sever the bond; Masters either escapes or is incarcerated; subject visits or corresponds during incarceration; Masters claims reform; cycle resumes. The bond outlasts every breach. It has outlasted, specifically: kidnapping her (multiple), using her as hostage against her own partner (multiple), endangering her life (multiple), psychologically operating on Ben Grimm whom she loves (constant), and — the foundational, eventually-disclosed atrocity — having murdered her biological father and disabled her.

**Disclosure and after.** When the truth of the sabotage entered her conscious knowledge (the exact issue of full disclosure is muddled across retcons; treat as a gradual disclosure across the late Bronze Age and modern era rather than a single revelation issue), her response was, again, *non-rupturing*. She did not pursue criminal complaint independent of his existing legal exposure. She did not refuse contact. She did not, on the record, confront him in the high-affect manner the disclosure would have warranted. The most that canon depicts is grieved, distanced, recalibrated continued contact. This is, on a forensic reading, *extraordinary*. It is also, on a psychodynamic reading, *over-determined*: she could not afford to lose him without losing the entire architecture of her childhood, including her own developmental memory of having-been-cared-for, and she had already lost her sight and her father; the cost of severing him was higher than the cost of metabolizing him.

**Dynamics.** Masters' caregiving of her as a child appears to have been **functionally adequate in the attachment-relevant domains**: consistent presence, responsive to her needs, materially providing, encouraging her artistic development (he was the natural conduit to clay), patient with the disability. He appears, in the limited domestic flashbacks, to have *loved* her — in a possessive, narrow, sentimentalized way that did not preclude using her — and this love was not faked. This is the part of the file that resists easy moralization: Masters was a real father to her in real ways. He was also her destroyer. Both are true, and the subject is the person on Earth who has lived longest inside that contradiction.

In the contemporary dynamic, contact is rationed and supervised-ish. She visits during incarcerations, accepts calls during free periods, declines to participate in or endorse his operations, and has been depicted as the only person whose judgment intermittently restrains him. He, for his part, is genuinely afraid of losing her good opinion — she is the only restraint on his behavior that is not a prison wall. The bond is *asymmetric in restraint power*: she has more power over him than he has over her, despite the appearance of the reverse.

**Trust / safety.** Operationally: she does **not** trust him with her partners, her children, her colleagues, her physical safety in his proximity during active villainy phases, or any information whose leak would harm the Fantastic Four. She **does** trust him to (a) not personally physically harm her, (b) tell her at least partial truth when directly asked across the table, (c) remember and honor the household-private rituals that constitute their shared past. The trust topology is fine-grained and consciously held; it is not the trust of a daughter who hasn't done the work, it is the trust of a daughter who has done all of it and arrived at calibrated terms.

**Failure mode.** *The schema this relationship installed is the seam Lyja exploited and any future hostile actor would target.* The "love the monster, see past the surface" template is, in its origin, a child's adaptive solution to the unbearable cognitive load of recognizing that her caregiver was her destroyer. Anything that confronts her with the *cost* of that template — its fungibility, its exploitation, its bleed into other relationships — destabilizes her. Masters himself is the standing reminder of this cost; her continued contact with him is, in part, a refusal to disown the template that has organized her adult life.

**Leverage.** *Maximum.* For a hostile actor: control of Masters' liberty, life, or wellbeing is direct leverage on the subject. She would not, on present evidence, betray Ben or the FF to save Masters' life — she has been tested at lower thresholds and held — but she would absorb considerable personal cost (her own freedom, her own injury) to spare him. She would also be uniquely susceptible to a *Masters-impersonation* operation, given the depth of haptic familiarity that would have to be falsified, but also given the disciplined emotional pre-loading any voice resembling his would receive. For a benevolent operator: Masters is the access vector to the subject's deepest unresolved material. He should not be approached as a route to her unless the operator is prepared to handle what comes back through that channel.

---

### 6.4 — BEN GRIMM (husband; chosen kin, treated here as origin-grade bond)

*Fully treated in Section 7 (Romantic & Pair-Bond). Included here only to flag that the marriage [FF #5, 2018, Slott] formally converted the longest-standing chosen attachment of her life into kin in the legal and ritual sense. He is, by every operational measure, her primary family. Cross-reference 7.1.*

---

### 6.5 — JO-VENN (adopted son; formerly of the Kree)

**Status:** Adopted child, post-Slott *FF* run, surviving Kree war-child taken in alongside N'Kalla. Living, in subject's primary household, school-age in apparent maturation rate (his species' development curve is unclear and the household has had to invent its own developmental milestones).

**History.** Jo-Venn enters the subject's life as a casualty of cosmic-scale political violence — a child engineered or raised as a combatant in the Kree-Skrull conflict, taken in by the Future Foundation environment after the relevant arcs. The adoption is unforced, deliberate, joint with Ben Grimm, and explicitly framed in text as *both* parents choosing both children together. The subject's voice in the decision is the deciding one; Ben follows her into the parenthood that he could not initiate but can sustain.

**Dynamics.** The subject's parenting style with Jo-Venn is **patient, haptic, declarative-but-non-coercive**, and unusually well-suited to a traumatized child of non-human biology. Her blindness is, here, an *asset*: she does not stare at his unfamiliar features, does not react with the micro-expressions of surprise or unease that human children of unusual appearance read with high acuity, and meets him initially through touch and voice without the visual othering that has likely shaped his entire prior experience of human adults. She has, in effect, the perfect sensory configuration for parenting an alien child in a human household. She also brings, from her own childhood, the specific competence of having *been* a child whose body marked her as different from her caregiving environment and who needed an adult to register her without flinching. She knows what it feels like to be parented by someone whose perceptual apparatus does not punish you for what you cannot help. She gives Jo-Venn that.

Specific parenting tells that the file should record: she reads to him by translation through Ben (sighted assistance) or via audio media she has curated for him; she has, on at least one depicted occasion, *taught him to work clay* — re-instantiating the workshop transmission that Masters once gave her, with the moral content cleansed; she addresses him by his full name, never a diminutive, treating his name as a sovereign object he brought with him; she does not push him to socialize with human children faster than he chooses to, but holds the door open.

**Trust / safety.** Mutual and forming. He trusts her physical presence absolutely. He is still learning that human adults do not switch on him; she is still learning the specific failure modes of a child raised as a weapon. The trust is real but young by parental standards.

**Failure mode.** The parental attachment system is **untested at scale** for the subject. Her composure under threats to *herself* is well-documented; her response to a credible, sustained threat to Jo-Venn or N'Kalla is not. Forecast: she would be more dangerous, more direct, and less containable in defense of the children than in defense of herself or Ben. This represents a new and largely unmapped vector of dysregulation in an otherwise extraordinarily regulated person.

**Leverage.** *High and rising.* The children are the newest pressure point in the file and have not yet been operationally exploited by adversaries within the canon. They should be considered the subject's most acute current vulnerability.

---

### 6.6 — N'KALLA (adopted daughter; formerly of the Skrulls)

**Status:** Adopted daughter, taken in concurrently with Jo-Venn. Living, household resident, post-trauma developmental trajectory in progress.

**History.** N'Kalla, a Skrull child paired with Jo-Venn in the Kree-Skrull narrative, enters the household by the same decision that brought Jo-Venn in. The species-political pairing of the two children — formerly enemy-coded, now siblings — is itself an artifact of the parents' (specifically the subject's) operating principle that *the surface does not define the soul*. The adoption of a Skrull child is, on the record, the single most psychologically loaded decision of the subject's parenting life, and it deserves its own paragraph.

**The Skrull dimension.** The subject was, for years of canonical time, **replaced by a Skrull** (Lyja). She lost a relationship, a marriage, and an interval of her own life to a Skrull operation. To then choose, decades later, to *raise a Skrull child as her own* is a deliberate non-symbolic act of refusing to let the species stand in for the individual. It is the subject's own operating principle applied to herself: *the surface — even the surface I have most reason to distrust — does not define the soul*. It is, in the technical sense, *integrative* behavior at the highest register: she has metabolized the harm Lyja did to her so completely that she can extend full parental love to a child of the same species without flinching, without conditional terms, without subtle withholding. This is rare. Most people, even psychologically healthy ones, retain a category-level wariness toward groups that have personally harmed them. The subject has done the work to dissolve that category back into individuals.

**Dynamics.** With N'Kalla specifically, the subject's parenting tells include: gentle correction when N'Kalla shapeshifts evasively rather than communicates verbally (the subject reframes the shift as a kind of speech and asks what it is *saying*, refusing to punish the morphology while requiring the communication); haptic contact in the form of hands-on-shoulders, hair-touching, face-touching when invited — recognizing that for a shapeshifting child, *being touched as oneself* is a sovereign experience the child can control; and the same clay-pedagogy extended to N'Kalla as to Jo-Venn, with the additional teaching that *what you make in clay holds its shape* — a quiet instruction in the value of chosen permanence to a child whose body does not insist on any.

**Trust / safety.** Mutual, deep, and unusually fast-forming given the parental backgrounds in play. N'Kalla appears to register the subject as safe in a way she has registered few adults; the subject's blindness and her acceptance of the species are both contributing factors.

**Failure mode.** Same as Jo-Venn: untested parental dysregulation under credible child-threat. Additionally: any operation that *uses* N'Kalla's shapeshifting against the family — coercion, abduction, impersonation — would activate both the parental defense system and the unresolved Lyja substrate simultaneously, and the interaction effects are unpredictable. This is the one scenario in the file where the subject's regulatory composure might predictably crack.

**Leverage.** High. See 6.5; the two children should be considered a single leverage object for operational purposes.

---

### 6.7 — THE FANTASTIC FOUR AS EXTENDED KIN

*Detailed treatment of Susan Storm-Richards, Reed Richards, and Johnny Storm appears in Section 7 (Allied & Chosen Bonds). Noted here only because the subject's marriage to Ben Grimm has, formally and informally, made the Richards-Storm household her extended family in the kin sense. She holds standing in their home, in their children's lives (Franklin and Valeria address her as a family elder), and at their table that is structurally indistinguishable from the standing of a sister-in-law in a tight extended family. The kin map cannot be drawn without that perimeter; it is drawn fully in the next section.*

---

### 6.8 — SYNTHESIS: THE SHAPE OF HER FAMILY

The kin matrix she has assembled by late midlife is **structurally compensatory to the kin matrix she was born into**. She was born to a father killed too soon, a mother gone too soon, and a stepfather who was secretly her destroyer. She has assembled, by choice, a husband whose body is a permanent visible referendum on the principle that destroyed her childhood (surface ≠ soul), two children adopted from species-categories that have, in different ways, been the agents of cosmic and personal harm to her, and an extended family of in-law kin who function as the steady horizontal scaffolding her vertical natal family never provided.

The pattern is not accidental. **She has rebuilt the family she lost, using the materials of the wounds that lost it to her.** Jacob's place is held by Ben (the dead-or-distant beloved man, here restored to her as living and present). The mother's vacancy is filled outward, by becoming one. Masters' place — the morally compromised parental figure — is held *by Masters himself*, who has not been replaced, only contained. The children she takes in are children of harm, the way she was. The family is, in its entirety, an act of authorship over her origin.

This is not pathology. This is, on the contrary, the signature of a person who has done the developmental work most people never finish. It is also, *because* it is so thoroughly authored, **uniquely targetable**: every figure in the matrix has been chosen for a reason that, if understood, gives an adversary the schematic. The dossier exists, in part, to ensure that those who would understand her for benevolent purposes do so before those who would understand her for hostile purposes complete the same map.

*— End Section 6. Continue to Section 7: Relationships II — Romantic, Allied & Chosen Bonds.*


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*Classification: Dossier Section 7 of 14 — Lateral & Affiliative Network Map*

A note on scope before the entries: the subject's affiliative network is *small by design and deep by practice*. She does not collect people. Across six decades of canonical surveillance, the documented circle of non-romantic, non-adversarial intimates does not exceed roughly a dozen names with meaningful contact frequency, and of those, perhaps five constitute genuine load-bearing relationships. This is consistent with the personality profile: a person whose perceptual modality is touch-and-attention does not scale relationally. She invests at depth or not at all. The corollary, important for any operational read on her, is that disturbance of any single one of these primary nodes registers as a structural event, not a perimeter event.

---

## 1. SUSAN STORM RICHARDS — Primary Female Anchor, Functional Sister

**History.** Contact established within hours of Alicia's introduction to the Baxter Building circle in 1962. The two women became confidantes effectively immediately, and Susan is the single most temporally consistent relationship in Alicia's adult life — outlasting Ben's transformations, the Skrull substitution, the Human Torch marriage, the Future Foundation reorganization, and every cosmic-scale dislocation of the team. If the file required a single name for "person Alicia would call at 3 a.m.," it is Susan.

**Dynamics.** The relationship operates on a near-perfect complementarity. Susan is the daylight strategist of the Richards household — managing schedules, mediating Reed's abstractions, holding the family's emotional ledger. Alicia is one of the very few people in Susan's adult life who *requires nothing of her in that managerial register* and who reliably returns attention rather than draining it. The dyad's signature pattern across the canon is the **kitchen-or-studio conversation** — depicted dozens of times from the Lee/Kirby run through North — in which Susan unloads a domestic or strategic concern and Alicia, hands occupied with clay or tea, listens, reflects back the part Susan was avoiding, and never offers unsolicited advice. The interpersonal economy is *Susan brings the problem, Alicia returns it cleaner*. This is therapeutic-grade listening, repeatedly demonstrated.

**Evolution.** Three discernible phases:
- *Phase I (1962–c. 1985), peer-sister*: roughly equal life stage, Alicia treated as quasi-team-member, frequent shared domestic scenes.
- *Phase II (1985–1995), strained*: Susan was among the FF members who failed to detect that her closest female friend had been replaced by a Skrull. The post-revelation reconciliation is canonically muted and, in this analyst's read, *never fully repaired in the textually visible record*. Susan carries the guilt; Alicia carries the knowledge of Susan's guilt. Both are too disciplined to discuss it.
- *Phase III (1995–present), restored-with-asterisk*: warm, frequent, but with a discernible boundary that did not exist in Phase I. Alicia no longer assumes the Baxter Building reads her presence accurately. She announces herself more, knocks where she once entered, makes more verbal anchors. This is a small behavioral residue and almost certainly unconscious — but it is in the record.

**Trust / safety.** Tier 1. Alicia has disclosed to Susan content not shared elsewhere, including (per implied dialogue across the Wieringo and Slott runs) the early ambivalence about adopting Jo-Venn and N'Kalla, and certain processing of the Phillip Masters revelations. Susan is one of perhaps two people Alicia permits to see her actively distressed.

**Failure mode.** The dyad's vulnerability is *competing loyalty during a Ben/Reed conflict*. When Reed's cure attempts have gone wrong, Susan's primary loyalty is to Reed and Alicia's is to Ben, and the two women have, on at least three documented occasions, sat through painful silences neither knew how to break. They do not fight; they go quiet. The friendship survives because both partners read silence accurately. A less skilled pair would have fractured.

**Leverage.** Anyone wishing to reach Alicia operationally via a trusted vector reaches her through Susan, not Ben. Susan is also the channel through which institutional Richards-family resources (medical, security, legal) flow to Alicia without Alicia having to ask Ben.

---

## 2. JOHNNY STORM — The Brother-In-Law Who Was Almost A Husband

**History.** This entry is structurally anomalous and must be handled with the file's full attention, because Johnny Storm occupies *two non-overlapping psychological positions* in Alicia's life: the man she did not marry (because the woman who married him was not her) and the family member she is now, by virtue of her marriage to Ben, permanently embedded with. The relationship is consequently the most complicated non-romantic tie in the file.

**Dynamics.** Pre-substitution (1962–c. 1985): younger-brother register on Johnny's side, indulgent-older-sister register on Alicia's. Alicia repeatedly defuses Johnny's adolescent flares throughout the Lee/Kirby and Thomas runs, treating him with affectionate impatience. Post-substitution and post-return: a sustained, careful, mutually protective awkwardness. Johnny carries the heaviest cognitive load of anyone in the FF on the Skrull matter — he *married* the impostor, fathered no child (the "Torus" child being a Skrull biological deception per *FF* #408), and on Alicia's return had to confront that his entire emotional life for years had been built on a person who was not the person he believed. Alicia's behavior toward him in the aftermath is among the most psychologically generous acts in her file: she explicitly absolved him, in dialogue, of having "loved the wrong woman." She framed his love as *real even if its object was false* — a sophisticated philosophical move that almost certainly prevented Johnny's complete decompensation.

**Evolution.** Phase I: indulgent older-sister. Phase II (during substitution): from Johnny's distorted perspective, marriage; from real Alicia's perspective, captivity. The relationship as it existed in published panels during this period is *not data about Alicia*. Phase III (post-return through Slott era): a re-negotiated kinship in which both parties studiously avoid the only topic that matters. Phase IV (Slott marriage to Ben and after): formal in-law status, which provides a structural cover for the unresolved material. Johnny defaults to humor; Alicia defaults to warmth; neither breaches.

**Trust / safety.** Tier 2 with an asterisk. She trusts Johnny's intentions absolutely and his judgment situationally. She does not disclose deep material to him. He does not invite it.

**Failure mode.** Alcohol or grief lowering Johnny's filter to the point that he attempts to talk about the marriage that wasn't. Alicia would not retaliate; she would withdraw, and the withdrawal would devastate him. Both seem aware of this; both manage around it.

**Leverage.** Johnny is the family member most likely to be manipulated *into* compromising Alicia's safety through misguided protective overreaction. He is also the family member who would notice fastest if she were replaced again — vigilance acquired through prior catastrophic failure. The Storm post-Skrull pattern recognition is a real asset and any threat actor must account for it.

---

## 3. BEN GRIMM'S AUNT PETUNIA & THE YANCY STREET EXTENDED FAMILY

**History.** Aunt Petunia Grimm (in the post-Byrne canonical clarification, an actual aunt rather than the colloquialism Ben long used) and the broader Grimm/Yancy Street network constitute Alicia's *acquired family of origin replacement*. She has been folded into Passover seders, Hanukkah dinners, and the periodic Yancy Street gatherings since at least the late Byrne era and continuously through the Slott marriage arc.

**Dynamics.** Alicia's reception in this milieu was immediate and total. The Yancy Street culture — working-class Jewish Lower East Side, oral and tactile rather than visual, dense with food and physical contact — is *exceptionally accommodating to a blind woman*. She does not need to be visually performed at; she is touched on the arm, talked to, fed, included by sound. The published scenes (Wolfman's *Marvel Two-in-One* run, the wedding-arc material in Slott's *FF*) consistently show Alicia *more relaxed in these settings than in the Baxter Building*, where surfaces are smooth and people move quietly across them. The Grimm family register matches her sensory operating system.

**Evolution.** A slow, steady deepening across forty published years. Notably accelerated by the marriage in *FF* #5 (2018), which formalized her standing and produced the only canonical depiction of Alicia being given a *family role title* (sister-in-law, aunt-by-marriage) outside her relationship to Ben himself.

**Trust / safety.** Tier 2, collectively. None of the Yancy Street individuals reach the depth of the Susan node, but the network as a whole functions as a *containment field* — a place where she is held without being scrutinized.

**Failure mode.** The network's protectiveness of Ben occasionally outweighs its perception of Alicia's autonomy. There have been moments (background dialogue, Slott run) of family members assuming Alicia would defer to Ben's preferences without consulting her, which she has corrected gently and effectively each time.

**Leverage.** Low. The network is geographically diffuse, culturally tight, and historically suspicious of outsiders. Operationally hard to penetrate, which makes it one of Alicia's safer affiliative zones.

---

## 4. FRANKLIN RICHARDS — Godson, Quasi-Nephew, Witness

**History.** Alicia has been present in Franklin's life from his infancy. She is one of the very small set of adults Franklin has known continuously across his entire existence, including through his reality-warping episodes, his various aging-and-de-aging arcs, and his periods of being raised in pocket dimensions of his own construction.

**Dynamics.** The relationship is shaped by a fact rarely articulated in canon but psychologically central: *Franklin, as a child reality-warper, could perceive things others could not, and Alicia, as a blind sculptor, perceived things others could not.* They share a non-visual epistemology. Multiple scenes across the Simonson, Waid, and Hickman runs depict Franklin bringing Alicia things to *touch* — toys, drawings rendered in clay at her suggestion, small constructions — rather than showing them. He learned, very young, that the way to share with Aunt Alicia was through her hands. This is an enormous accommodation for a child to make spontaneously, and the fact that he made it is its own data about both of them.

**Evolution.** Caretaker-to-toddler in the early years; trusted adult-confidante through the Heroes Reborn / Counter-Earth period; co-equal in some respects during the Hickman cosmic arcs when Franklin's powers placed him functionally beyond most adult comprehension. Alicia's response to encountering a near-omnipotent godson was *to treat him exactly as she had when he was four* — same voice, same physical contact, same patience. This may be the single most stabilizing input Franklin received during his god-tier phase.

**Trust / safety.** Tier 1 from Franklin's side, Tier 2 from Alicia's (she protects him rather than confiding in him; the asymmetry is appropriate).

**Failure mode.** Franklin's powers have, on at least one occasion (the Hickman material), made him capable of *restoring* things — including, theoretically, sight. There is no canonical scene of him offering this to Alicia, and the absence is significant. Either he has offered off-panel and been declined, or he has correctly intuited that the offer itself would be a small violation. Either way, the dynamic is stable but contains a latent question neither has surfaced.

**Leverage.** Anyone threatening Franklin elicits one of the very few documented displays of Alicia's *anger register*. She has been depicted physically inserting herself between Franklin and perceived threats in domestic scenes (the Onslaught aftermath, the Counter-Earth return). Threat actors should treat Franklin and Valeria as *category-one* vulnerabilities in Alicia's response profile.

---

## 5. VALERIA RICHARDS — Goddaughter, Intellectual Foil

**History.** Valeria's existence has been canonically complicated (the Doom arc, the unborn-then-aged-up retcon, the Future Foundation tenure). Throughout, Alicia has been a consistent adult presence.

**Dynamics.** Where the Franklin relationship is tactile-perceptual, the Valeria relationship is *verbal-philosophical*. Valeria, hyperintelligent and frequently bored, finds in Alicia an adult who *asks her questions she cannot answer with data*. Documented exchanges (Hickman, Slott runs) show Valeria attempting to explain a technical problem and Alicia redirecting to the human question underneath it — a move Valeria visibly resents and then visibly uses.
